1db796785343406698ae6bec14f65280 Episode 5: Dropping Like Flies Thu, 24 Apr 2014 19:00:00 -0000 http://feeds.thisiscriminal.com/~r/CriminalShow/~3/7CZiII6_3c4/225540 Every year for the past few years, tens of thousand of flytraps have gone missing – from the wild, from gardens, from nurseries. And, really, nobody knows where they go. What’s cropped up in rural North Carolina is essentially a Venus Flytrap crime ring — with lackies, middle men, and a mysterious end buyer who’s perpetuating the market.

"episode-83-the-mothers-01-26-2018</> "content": "<p data-pm-context=\"[]\">There is a group in Durham, NC called “Parents of Murdered Children.” This week, we meet three of its members.</p>\n<p data-pm-context=\"[]\">Photojournalist <span class=\"il\">Justin</span> <span class=\"il\">Cook</span> has spent ten years documenting the impact of homicide in Durham, North Carolina. You can see more of his work <a href=\"http://www.justincookphoto.com/\">here</a>.</p>\n<div id=\"attachment_2204\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2204\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2204\" src=\"http://www.thisiscriminal.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/2018_MADE_IN_DURHAM_001A-1024x682.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"682\" srcset=\"https://thisiscriminal.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/2018_MADE_IN_DURHAM_001A-1024x682.jpg 1024w, https://thisiscriminal.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/2018_MADE_IN_DURHAM_001A-300x200.jpg 300w, https://thisiscriminal.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/2018_MADE_IN_DURHAM_001A-768x512.jpg 768w, https://thisiscriminal.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/2018_MADE_IN_DURHAM_001A-670x446.jpg 670w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2204\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Photographer <span class=\"il\">Justin</span> <span class=\"il\">Cook</span> writes: <i>Joslin Simms’s son, Rayburn, 30, was killed in 2005. The case remains unsolved.</i><i> She says: “Since Ray been murdered, I have nightmares. I dream of him in the morgue and when they are cutting his body I wake up because I can feel the knife cutting me.”  <span class=\"aBn\" tabindex=\"0\" data-term=\"goog_75129272\"><span class=\"aQJ\">Thirteen years later</span></span>, </i><i>Joslin remains maimed by her grief. She calls it a “walking death.” But her grief also propels her to speak out about gun violence, poverty and gentrification in her community. </i></p></div>\n<p> </p>\n<div id=\"attachment_2205\" to equal that of the escape of William and Ellen Craft; and future historians and poets would tell...</>, "slug": "episode-59-in-plain-sight-1-20-2017</> "content": "<p>In 1849, abolitionist and attorney Wendell Phillips wrote: “We should look in vain through the most trying times of our revolutionary history for an incident of courage and noble daring to equal that of the escape of William and Ellen Craft; and future historians and poets would tell this story as one of the most thrilling in the nation’s annals, and millions would read it, with admiration of the hero and heroine of the story.” Unfortunately, almost 170 years later, William and Ellen Craft aren’t well known anymore. Today, we have the story of this couple’s incredible escape from slavery, the abolitionist pastor Theodore Parker who married the Crafts, and their founding of the Woodville Co-operative Farm School.</p>\n<p>Read the Crafts’ book: <a href=\"http://www.gutenberg.org/ebooks/585\"><em>Running a Thousand Miles for Freedom</em></a></p>\n<p>Barbara McCaskill wrote about William and Ellen Craft One Sunday, Michael McIntosh went to visit his son and was turned away because, he was told, prison officials “did not know” where his son was. He spent the next six weeks searching for his son, only to find him in the hospital with severe injuries. And Michael McIntosh’s son wasn’t the only one who had been hurt at the facility.</p>\n<p>Jody Owns of the Southern Poverty Law center launched an investigation and found that Walnut Grove was such a violent prison that one Federal Judge called it “a cesspool of unconstitutional and inhuman acts.” Today, we have the story of an especially troubled youth prison, the for-profit corporation, Cornell Companies, that managed it, and the small town that relied on it.</p>\n<p><em><a href=\"https://www.justice.gov/sites/default/files/crt/legacy/2012/04/09/walnutgrovefl.pdf\">The U.S. Department of sensational writing style. People thought no jail was strong enough to keep him, but then in 1895 he was sentenced to Philadelphia’s Eastern State Penitentiary. At Eastern State, Frankford became the victim of a strange practice: the prison doctor, Dr. John Bacon, dissected his body and removed his brain. The Frankford case would just be one of many other in the region and would illuminate an underground cadaver network supplying medical schools across the state of Pennsylvania.</p>\n<p>Reporter Elana Nelson Johnson and Signe Waller-Foxworth remember shouting at armed Klansmen and burning a confederate flag, until eventually police forced the KKK inside and the standoff ended without violence. The labor organizers felt they’d won a small victory, and planned a much bigger anti-Klan demonstration in Greensboro, North Carolina. They advertised with the slogan: “Death to the Klan” and set the date for November 3rd, 1979.</p>\n<p>As protestors assembled, a caravan of nine cars appeared, and a man in a pick-up truck yelled: “You asked for the Klan! Now you’ve got them!” Thirty-nine shots were fired in eighty-eight seconds, and five protestors were killed. The city of Greensboro is still grappling with the complicated legacy of that day.</p>\n<hr />\n<p><em><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Greensboro Truth and Reconciliation Commission’s </span><a style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Today, Reverend Nelson Johnson is a pastor with Faith Community Church and serves as the Executive Director for the </span><a href=\"http://www.belovedcommunitycenter.org/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Beloved Community Center of Greensboro</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, which advocates for social and economic justice.</span></em></p>\n<p><em><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Signe Waller-Foxworth is the author of  </span></em><a href=\"http://www.indiebound.org/book/9780742513655\"><span Courts have ruled that “flipping the bird” is a form of speech protected by the First Amendment. It’s not a crime to be obnoxious. She attended the Cambridge Nursing School, and established a successful private nursing career in Boston. Said to be cheerful, funny and excellent with her patients, nothing about “Jolly Jane” suggested she could be “the most notorious woman poisoner of modern times” responsible for the death of at least 35 people. She would later be committed to the Taunton Insane Asylum.</p>\n<p> </p>\n<div id=\"attachment_1008\" style=\"width: 597px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1008\" class=\"wp-image-1008\" src=\"http://thisiscriminal.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/FullSizeRender-1-e1457064836607-752x1024.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"587\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://thisiscriminal.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/FullSizeRender-1-e1457064836607-752x1024.jpg 752w, https://thisiscriminal.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/FullSizeRender-1-e1457064836607-220x300.jpg 220w, https://thisiscriminal.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/FullSizeRender-1-e1457064836607.jpg 1116w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 587px) 100vw, 587px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-1008\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">“Jolly” Jane Toppan</p></div>\n<p> </p>\n<div id=\"attachment_1006\" style=\"width: 958px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1006\" class=\"wp-image-1006 size-large\" src=\"http://thisiscriminal.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/FullSizeRender-2-948x1024.jpg\" alt=\"FullSizeRender (2)\" width=\"948\" height=\"1024\" srcset=\"https://thisiscriminal.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/FullSizeRender-2-948x1024.jpg 948w, https://thisiscriminal.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/FullSizeRender-2-278x300.jpg 278w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 948px) 100vw, 948px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-1006\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Death certificates for Alden Davis and his daughter Genevieve.
